The Distinction Between Existence and Necessity: Objection and Refutation
The author presents an objection and its refutation concerning the distinction between existence and necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why distinguishing existence from necessity as two real attributes leads to logical absurdities such as circularity and infinite regress.

Core Idea
Existence and necessity cannot be two distinct real attributes in God.

In theological discussions, it is often objected that existence and necessity are distinct because we perceive a conceptual difference. This lesson presents that objection and the classical refutation showing that if they were truly distinct, it would lead to impossible consequences. Understanding this refutation is crucial for grasping the unity of God's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector claims existence and necessity are different because what is shared (existence) differs from what distinguishes (necessity). Notice the key distinction between 'existent necessary' and 'existent existent'.
2
Follow the refutation's structure
The refutation considers two possibilities: no entailment or entailment between existence and necessity. Each possibility leads to absurdity: either separation of existence from necessity, or circularity, or infinite regress. Trace the argument step by step.
Pay attention to the terms 'dawr' (circularity) and 'tasalsul' (infinite regress).
3
Examine the first marginal note
The author notes that the objection relies on existence being univocal, but in reality existence is analogical (tashkik). This undermines the objection's foundation.
The example of sunlight and other lights illustrates the point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الواجب لذاته يساوى سائر الموجودات فى أصل الوجود ويخالفها في الوجوب ومابه الاشتراك غير ما به الامتياز فالوجود غير الوجوب ، ولأنا ندرك التفرقة بين قولنا موجود واجب وبين قولنا موجود موجود ، ولو كان الوجود هو الوجوب ما بقى الفرق ، وإذا ثبت أن الوجود غير الوجوب فنقول إما أن لا يكون بينهما ملازمة أو يكون والأول محال وإلا يصح انفكاك كل واحد منهما من الآخر ، فيمكن انفكاك ذلك الوجود عن الوجوب ، وكل ما كان كذلك استحال أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، وأيضاً يمكن انفكاك الوجوب عن الوجود وذلك لأن الوجود محال ، إذا الوجوب نعت الوجود ويستحيل حصول النعت دون المنعوت . وأما الثانى وهو أن يكون بينهما ملازمة فمن المحال أن يكون كل واحد منهما مفتقراً إلى الآخر لاستحالة الدور ، ومحال أن يكون الوجود مستلزما للوجوب والأفكل موجود واجب هذا خلف (1) . ولانه يلزم كون الوجوب معاولا وكل معلول ممكن لذاته واجب بعلته فقبل هذا الوجوب وجوب إلى غير النهاية وهو محال (۲) • آخر ومحال أن يكون الوجوب مستلزما للوجود لأن الوجوب نعت الوجود وكيفيته فيكون مفتقراً إليه فلو كان الوجود مفتقراً إليه يلزم الدور وأنه محال، ومحال أن يكونا معلولى علة لأن تلك العلة إما أن تكون موصوفة بهما غير ترجيح ، هذا على قول من يقول إن الصفات لا توجد إلا مع الوجود، وأيضاً مم عرفت أنه لا مر جمع هناك غاية ما في الباب أنك تقول لا دليل على ذلك ولا يجب من عدم معرفته عدمه ، وأصحاب هذه المذاهب لما فسروا الذات بما يصح أن يعلم ويخبر عنه لزمهم القول بأن الذرات مشتركة ، والحق أن صحة أنه يعلم ويخبر عنه من لوازم الذات أو عوارضه لأنفسها . (1) أقول : لو كان الوجود المشترك يدل على الموجودات بالتواطؤ لزم من كونه مستلزما للوجوب في موضع كون كل موجود مستاز ما له وليس الأمر كذلك، فإنه يدل عليها بالتشكيك ، والمعانى المشتركة على سبيل التشكيك لا يقتضى استلزام بعضها لشيء استلزام غير ذلك البعض لذلك الشيء مثلا نور الشمس يستلزم زوال العشى وسائر الأنوار لا يقتضيه لكون النور بين نورها وبين سائر الأنوار بالتشكيك . ( ۲ ) أقول : لا يلزم من كون الوجوب لازماكونه معلولا ، والحق أن الوجوب والإمكان والامتناع مور معقولة تحصل في العقل من إسناد التصورات إلى الوجود الخارجى وهى في أنفسها محاولات للعقل الشرط لإستاد المذكور ، وليست بموجودات في الخارج حتى تكون علة الأمور التى يسند إليها أو معلولا لها كما أن تصور ، زيد ، وإن كان محلولا لمن يتصوره لا يكون علة لزيد ولا معلولا له ، وكون الشيء واجبا في الخارج وهو كونه بحيث إذا عقله عاقل مسند إلى الوجود الخارجي لزم فى عقله معقول وهو الوجوب . أو صفة لهما أو لا موصوفه ولاصفة والأول محال وإلا لسكان ما ليس موجود ولا واجب هلة الموجوب والوجود لكن كون ما ليس بموجود ولا واجب علة للوجوب والوجود محال ، لأن ما ليس بموجود فهو معدوم ، فكون المعدوم هلة للوسوب والوجود هذا خلف ، ولأنه يلزم كون الوجوب معاولا وهو محال على ما تقدم . والثانى محال وإلا عاد الإشكال في كيفية ذلك اللزوم، والثالث محال لأنه يلزم أن يكون الموجود الواجب اذاته مفتقراً إلى علة منفصلة وهذا خلف (۱) لا يقال : الوجوب ساى . لانا نقول إنه يتأكد الوجود به والشيء لا يتأكد بنقيضه ، ولأنه يقتضى اللا وجوب بالدى هو عدمى لكونه محمولا على العدم فيكون وجوديا ، سلمنا كونه سلبيا لكن يستحيل أن يكون المقتضى للوجود هو الوجوب لامتناع كون العدم مقتضيا للوجود ولا بالعكس ، وإلا كان كل موجود واجبا . والجواب : أنه بناء على كون الوجود مشتركا بين الواجب والممكن وهو محال على ما تقدم (٢) . (1) أقول : هذا كله إنما يلزم على تقدير كون الوجود والوجوب موجودين في الخارج متباينين وذلك الحال. (٢) أقول : إذا كان الوجوب سلبيا لا يلزم منه أن يكون نقيضا للوجود ، وإن السلي هو سلب شيء عن شيء أو سلب الشيء من الوجود لا يكون خمل العدم عليه ، وأيضاً إن كان الوجوب واللا وجوب نقيضين يعنى يفتسمان جميع الاحتمالات والوجود والعدم كذلك ، وكان العدم محمولا على اللا وجوب فلا يلزم أن يكون الوجود محمولا على الوجوب حملا كليا ، لأنه من الجائز أن يكون بعض ما هو وجوب عدميا أيضاً، فإن الممكن العام والممتنع نقيضان بالوجه المذكور والممتنع عدمى ، فلا يجب أن يكون كل ماهو ممكن بالإمكان العام وجوديا بل بعضه وجودى وبعضه عدمى وهذا ما يستعمل فى هذا الكتاب فى مواضع وفيه غلط فاحش على ماتبين ، وعلى أن الشيء منها مع النقيض وشرائطه المذكورة في أكثر كتبه . وقوله : على تقدير كون الوجوب سلبيا يستحيل أن يكون المقتضى للوجود هو الوجوب لامتناع كون العدم مقتضيا لثبوت جعل اللمبى عدما ، وكثير من الأمور السلبية يقتضى أمرا وجوديا كما سيجيء بيانه وحكم أن هذه الاعتراضات مبنى على كون الوجود مشتركا حكم غير صحيح .
For it is said: The Necessary Being is equal to other existents in the essence of existence and differs from them in necessity, and what is shared is other than what distinguishes, so existence is other than necessity. And because we perceive a difference between our statement 'existent necessary' and our statement 'existent existent', and if existence were necessity, no difference would remain. And if it is established that existence is other than necessity, we say: either there is no entailment between them, or there is. The first is impossible, otherwise each could be separated from the other, so that existence could be separated from necessity, and everything that is such cannot be necessary by itself. Also, necessity could be separated from existence, because existence is impossible? (unclear) since necessity is an attribute of existence and it is impossible for the attribute to exist without the subject. As for the second—that there is entailment between them—it is impossible for each to be dependent on the other due to the impossibility of circularity; and impossible for existence to entail necessity, otherwise every existent would be necessary—this is contrary (1). And because it would necessitate that necessity is an effect, and every effect is possible by itself and necessary by its cause, so before this necessity there would be necessity ad infinitum, which is impossible (2). • Another: And impossible for necessity to entail existence, because necessity is an attribute and qualifier of existence, so it is dependent on it; if existence were dependent on it, circularity would follow, and it is impossible. And impossible for both to be effects of a cause, because that cause is either described by them? (unclear), this according to those who say that attributes exist only with existence. Also, you know that there is no ? there; the upshot is that you say there is no proof for that, and its non-existence is not necessitated by ignorance of it. The proponents of these views, when they interpreted essence as that which can be known and reported about, were forced to say that atoms are common. The truth is that the validity of being known and reported about is among the concomitants of essence or its accidents in themselves. (1) I say: If shared existence signified existents by univocity, then its entailing necessity in one case would entail that every existent has its necessity, but it is not so; rather it signifies by analogy, and common meanings by analogy do not require that entailment of some of them for something is the same as entailment of others for that thing. For example, sunlight entails the departure of night, but other lights do not entail it, because the light of the sun is related to other lights by analogy. (2) I say: The fact that necessity is a concomitant does not necessitate that it is an effect. The truth is that necessity, possibility, and impossibility are mental concepts obtained in the mind from relating concepts to external existence, and they are in themselves constructs of the mind condition for that relating? They are not existents externally so as to be causes of the things to which they are related or effects of them, just as the concept 'Zayd', even if it is analyzed by one who conceives it, is neither a cause of Zayd nor an effect of him. And the thing being necessary externally means that if a rational being conceives it relating it to external existence, a concept—namely necessity—necessarily arises in his mind. Or an attribute for both, or not described and no attribute? The first is impossible, otherwise what is not existent and not necessary would be a cause of necessity and existence, but that what is not existent and not necessary is a cause of necessity and existence is impossible, because what is not existent is nonexistent, so the nonexistent being a cause of necessity and existence is contradictory; and because it would necessitate that necessity is an effect, and it is impossible as previously. The second is impossible, otherwise the problem would return to how that entailment occurs; the third is impossible because it would necessitate that the Necessary Being is dependent on a separate cause—this is contradictory (1). It cannot be said: Necessity is negative? because we say: it strengthens existence, and a thing is not strengthened by its opposite; and because it necessitates non-necessity? which is non-existential, since it is predicated on nonexistence, so it becomes existential. We grant that it is privative, but it is impossible that necessity be that which necessitates existence, because nonexistence cannot necessitate existence, nor vice versa, otherwise every existent would be necessary. The answer: That is based on the assumption that existence is common between the necessary and the possible, and it is impossible as previously (2). (1) I say: All this only follows on the assumption that existence and necessity are existents externally as distinct (attributes), and that is the case. (2) I say: If necessity is privative, it does not necessitate that it be opposite to existence; and the privative is the negation of a thing from a thing or the negation of a thing from existence, so it is not predicated on nonexistence. Also, if necessity and non-necessity are opposites, meaning they exhaust all possibilities, and existence and nonexistence are likewise, and nonexistence is predicated on non-necessity, it does not necessitate that existence be predicated on necessity universally, because it is possible that some of what is necessity is also nonexistential; indeed the universal possible and the impossible are opposites in the mentioned respect, and the impossible is nonexistential, so not everything that is possible in the universal sense is existential; rather some of it is existential and some is nonexistential. This is used in this book in places, and in it there is a manifest error as has been clarified, and that the thing with its opposite and its conditions mentioned in most of his books. And his statement: On the assumption that necessity is privative, it is impossible for that which necessitates existence to be necessity, because nonexistence cannot necessitate the affirmation of making the thing nonexistent?; and many privative matters necessitate an existential matter as will be explained. And the judgment that these objections are based on existence being common is an incorrect judgment.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a complex objection-response argument distinguishing existence (wujud) from necessity (wujub). The objector claims they are distinct because they differ in predication. The author refutes that any real distinction leads to absurdities like circularity or infinite regress. He then provides his own view, supported by marginal notes, that necessity is a mental concept, not a real attribute. The final part addresses a further objection that necessity is privative, and the author argues that the entire debate rests on the false assumption that 'existence' is univocally predicated of God and creatures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think existence and necessity are two distinct real attributes in God.
Correction: The refutation shows that if they were distinct, it leads to absurdities; the author later explains that necessity is a mental concept, not an external attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, what would happen if existence entailed necessity?
A) Every existent would be necessary.
B) Existence would be separated from necessity.
C) There would be no problem.
D) Necessity would be an effect.

Key Takeaway
Existence and necessity cannot be distinct real attributes because that leads to logical absurdities; the objection is based on a false assumption of univocity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence and necessity are not distinct parts but one reality, how does that confront any tendency in your heart to think of God as composed of separate 'pieces'? Will you today abandon that mental image and worship Him as indivisible?
?
The objector's plausible argument arises from human logic. When you find a rational objection to God's nature, do you instinctively trust your reasoning over revelation? This passage shows even the strongest logic fails without the right assumptions. What assumption about God are you holding that you need to surrender to His transcendence?
?
The proof shows that distinguishing existence from necessity leads to absurdities like infinite regress. In your spiritual life, have you ever made a distinction about God that actually pushed Him further from your heart, making Him feel less immediate? Commit to removing one such mental barrier today.

Allah's Existence
advanced
10 min
Necessity as a Mental Concept and the Privative Objection
The author explains the nature of necessity and refutes the privative objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessity is not a real attribute but a mental concept, and how the privative objection is resolved by the analogical nature of existence.

Core Idea
Necessity is a mental concept, not an external attribute.

After refuting the distinction between existence and necessity as real attributes, the author presents his positive view: necessity, possibility, and impossibility are mental constructs arising from relating concepts to existence. This lesson explores that view and addresses the objection that necessity is privative.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's positive claim
The author states that necessity is a mental concept like the concept of Zayd. Understand the analogy: just as the concept of Zayd is not a real attribute, necessity is not an external existent.
2
Follow the argument against the privative objection
The objection claims necessity is privative (negative). The author argues that even if it were privative, it does not imply opposition to existence or that it necessitates nonexistence.
Note the distinction between privative and negative.
3
Understand the final conclusion
The entire debate is based on the false assumption that existence is univocal. Since existence is analogical, the objections are invalid.

فإن قيل : الواجب لذاته يساوى سائر الموجودات فى أصل الوجود ويخالفها في الوجوب ومابه الاشتراك غير ما به الامتياز فالوجود غير الوجوب ، ولأنا ندرك التفرقة بين قولنا موجود واجب وبين قولنا موجود موجود ، ولو كان الوجود هو الوجوب ما بقى الفرق ، وإذا ثبت أن الوجود غير الوجوب فنقول إما أن لا يكون بينهما ملازمة أو يكون والأول محال وإلا يصح انفكاك كل واحد منهما من الآخر ، فيمكن انفكاك ذلك الوجود عن الوجوب ، وكل ما كان كذلك استحال أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، وأيضاً يمكن انفكاك الوجوب عن الوجود وذلك لأن الوجود محال ، إذا الوجوب نعت الوجود ويستحيل حصول النعت دون المنعوت . وأما الثانى وهو أن يكون بينهما ملازمة فمن المحال أن يكون كل واحد منهما مفتقراً إلى الآخر لاستحالة الدور ، ومحال أن يكون الوجود مستلزما للوجوب والأفكل موجود واجب هذا خلف (1) . ولانه يلزم كون الوجوب معاولا وكل معلول ممكن لذاته واجب بعلته فقبل هذا الوجوب وجوب إلى غير النهاية وهو محال (۲) • آخر ومحال أن يكون الوجوب مستلزما للوجود لأن الوجوب نعت الوجود وكيفيته فيكون مفتقراً إليه فلو كان الوجود مفتقراً إليه يلزم الدور وأنه محال، ومحال أن يكونا معلولى علة لأن تلك العلة إما أن تكون موصوفة بهما غير ترجيح ، هذا على قول من يقول إن الصفات لا توجد إلا مع الوجود، وأيضاً مم عرفت أنه لا مر جمع هناك غاية ما في الباب أنك تقول لا دليل على ذلك ولا يجب من عدم معرفته عدمه ، وأصحاب هذه المذاهب لما فسروا الذات بما يصح أن يعلم ويخبر عنه لزمهم القول بأن الذرات مشتركة ، والحق أن صحة أنه يعلم ويخبر عنه من لوازم الذات أو عوارضه لأنفسها . (1) أقول : لو كان الوجود المشترك يدل على الموجودات بالتواطؤ لزم من كونه مستلزما للوجوب في موضع كون كل موجود مستاز ما له وليس الأمر كذلك، فإنه يدل عليها بالتشكيك ، والمعانى المشتركة على سبيل التشكيك لا يقتضى استلزام بعضها لشيء استلزام غير ذلك البعض لذلك الشيء مثلا نور الشمس يستلزم زوال العشى وسائر الأنوار لا يقتضيه لكون النور بين نورها وبين سائر الأنوار بالتشكيك . ( ۲ ) أقول : لا يلزم من كون الوجوب لازماكونه معلولا ، والحق أن الوجوب والإمكان والامتناع مور معقولة تحصل في العقل من إسناد التصورات إلى الوجود الخارجى وهى في أنفسها محاولات للعقل الشرط لإستاد المذكور ، وليست بموجودات في الخارج حتى تكون علة الأمور التى يسند إليها أو معلولا لها كما أن تصور ، زيد ، وإن كان محلولا لمن يتصوره لا يكون علة لزيد ولا معلولا له ، وكون الشيء واجبا في الخارج وهو كونه بحيث إذا عقله عاقل مسند إلى الوجود الخارجي لزم فى عقله معقول وهو الوجوب . أو صفة لهما أو لا موصوفه ولاصفة والأول محال وإلا لسكان ما ليس موجود ولا واجب هلة الموجوب والوجود لكن كون ما ليس بموجود ولا واجب علة للوجوب والوجود محال ، لأن ما ليس بموجود فهو معدوم ، فكون المعدوم هلة للوسوب والوجود هذا خلف ، ولأنه يلزم كون الوجوب معاولا وهو محال على ما تقدم . والثانى محال وإلا عاد الإشكال في كيفية ذلك اللزوم، والثالث محال لأنه يلزم أن يكون الموجود الواجب اذاته مفتقراً إلى علة منفصلة وهذا خلف (۱) لا يقال : الوجوب ساى . لانا نقول إنه يتأكد الوجود به والشيء لا يتأكد بنقيضه ، ولأنه يقتضى اللا وجوب بالدى هو عدمى لكونه محمولا على العدم فيكون وجوديا ، سلمنا كونه سلبيا لكن يستحيل أن يكون المقتضى للوجود هو الوجوب لامتناع كون العدم مقتضيا للوجود ولا بالعكس ، وإلا كان كل موجود واجبا . والجواب : أنه بناء على كون الوجود مشتركا بين الواجب والممكن وهو محال على ما تقدم (٢) . (1) أقول : هذا كله إنما يلزم على تقدير كون الوجود والوجوب موجودين في الخارج متباينين وذلك الحال. (٢) أقول : إذا كان الوجوب سلبيا لا يلزم منه أن يكون نقيضا للوجود ، وإن السلي هو سلب شيء عن شيء أو سلب الشيء من الوجود لا يكون خمل العدم عليه ، وأيضاً إن كان الوجوب واللا وجوب نقيضين يعنى يفتسمان جميع الاحتمالات والوجود والعدم كذلك ، وكان العدم محمولا على اللا وجوب فلا يلزم أن يكون الوجود محمولا على الوجوب حملا كليا ، لأنه من الجائز أن يكون بعض ما هو وجوب عدميا أيضاً، فإن الممكن العام والممتنع نقيضان بالوجه المذكور والممتنع عدمى ، فلا يجب أن يكون كل ماهو ممكن بالإمكان العام وجوديا بل بعضه وجودى وبعضه عدمى وهذا ما يستعمل فى هذا الكتاب فى مواضع وفيه غلط فاحش على ماتبين ، وعلى أن الشيء منها مع النقيض وشرائطه المذكورة في أكثر كتبه . وقوله : على تقدير كون الوجوب سلبيا يستحيل أن يكون المقتضى للوجود هو الوجوب لامتناع كون العدم مقتضيا لثبوت جعل اللمبى عدما ، وكثير من الأمور السلبية يقتضى أمرا وجوديا كما سيجيء بيانه وحكم أن هذه الاعتراضات مبنى على كون الوجود مشتركا حكم غير صحيح .
For it is said: The Necessary Being is equal to other existents in the essence of existence and differs from them in necessity, and what is shared is other than what distinguishes, so existence is other than necessity. And because we perceive a difference between our statement 'existent necessary' and our statement 'existent existent', and if existence were necessity, no difference would remain. And if it is established that existence is other than necessity, we say: either there is no entailment between them, or there is. The first is impossible, otherwise each could be separated from the other, so that existence could be separated from necessity, and everything that is such cannot be necessary by itself. Also, necessity could be separated from existence, because existence is impossible? (unclear) since necessity is an attribute of existence and it is impossible for the attribute to exist without the subject. As for the second—that there is entailment between them—it is impossible for each to be dependent on the other due to the impossibility of circularity; and impossible for existence to entail necessity, otherwise every existent would be necessary—this is contrary (1). And because it would necessitate that necessity is an effect, and every effect is possible by itself and necessary by its cause, so before this necessity there would be necessity ad infinitum, which is impossible (2). • Another: And impossible for necessity to entail existence, because necessity is an attribute and qualifier of existence, so it is dependent on it; if existence were dependent on it, circularity would follow, and it is impossible. And impossible for both to be effects of a cause, because that cause is either described by them? (unclear), this according to those who say that attributes exist only with existence. Also, you know that there is no ? there; the upshot is that you say there is no proof for that, and its non-existence is not necessitated by ignorance of it. The proponents of these views, when they interpreted essence as that which can be known and reported about, were forced to say that atoms are common. The truth is that the validity of being known and reported about is among the concomitants of essence or its accidents in themselves. (1) I say: If shared existence signified existents by univocity, then its entailing necessity in one case would entail that every existent has its necessity, but it is not so; rather it signifies by analogy, and common meanings by analogy do not require that entailment of some of them for something is the same as entailment of others for that thing. For example, sunlight entails the departure of night, but other lights do not entail it, because the light of the sun is related to other lights by analogy. (2) I say: The fact that necessity is a concomitant does not necessitate that it is an effect. The truth is that necessity, possibility, and impossibility are mental concepts obtained in the mind from relating concepts to external existence, and they are in themselves constructs of the mind condition for that relating? They are not existents externally so as to be causes of the things to which they are related or effects of them, just as the concept 'Zayd', even if it is analyzed by one who conceives it, is neither a cause of Zayd nor an effect of him. And the thing being necessary externally means that if a rational being conceives it relating it to external existence, a concept—namely necessity—necessarily arises in his mind. Or an attribute for both, or not described and no attribute? The first is impossible, otherwise what is not existent and not necessary would be a cause of necessity and existence, but that what is not existent and not necessary is a cause of necessity and existence is impossible, because what is not existent is nonexistent, so the nonexistent being a cause of necessity and existence is contradictory; and because it would necessitate that necessity is an effect, and it is impossible as previously. The second is impossible, otherwise the problem would return to how that entailment occurs; the third is impossible because it would necessitate that the Necessary Being is dependent on a separate cause—this is contradictory (1). It cannot be said: Necessity is negative? because we say: it strengthens existence, and a thing is not strengthened by its opposite; and because it necessitates non-necessity? which is non-existential, since it is predicated on nonexistence, so it becomes existential. We grant that it is privative, but it is impossible that necessity be that which necessitates existence, because nonexistence cannot necessitate existence, nor vice versa, otherwise every existent would be necessary. The answer: That is based on the assumption that existence is common between the necessary and the possible, and it is impossible as previously (2). (1) I say: All this only follows on the assumption that existence and necessity are existents externally as distinct (attributes), and that is the case. (2) I say: If necessity is privative, it does not necessitate that it be opposite to existence; and the privative is the negation of a thing from a thing or the negation of a thing from existence, so it is not predicated on nonexistence. Also, if necessity and non-necessity are opposites, meaning they exhaust all possibilities, and existence and nonexistence are likewise, and nonexistence is predicated on non-necessity, it does not necessitate that existence be predicated on necessity universally, because it is possible that some of what is necessity is also nonexistential; indeed the universal possible and the impossible are opposites in the mentioned respect, and the impossible is nonexistential, so not everything that is possible in the universal sense is existential; rather some of it is existential and some is nonexistential. This is used in this book in places, and in it there is a manifest error as has been clarified, and that the thing with its opposite and its conditions mentioned in most of his books. And his statement: On the assumption that necessity is privative, it is impossible for that which necessitates existence to be necessity, because nonexistence cannot necessitate the affirmation of making the thing nonexistent?; and many privative matters necessitate an existential matter as will be explained. And the judgment that these objections are based on existence being common is an incorrect judgment.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a complex objection-response argument distinguishing existence (wujud) from necessity (wujub). The objector claims they are distinct because they differ in predication. The author refutes that any real distinction leads to absurdities like circularity or infinite regress. He then provides his own view, supported by marginal notes, that necessity is a mental concept, not a real attribute. The final part addresses a further objection that necessity is privative, and the author argues that the entire debate rests on the false assumption that 'existence' is univocally predicated of God and creatures.

الإمكان
الامتناع
المعقول
التشكيك

السلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think necessity is a negative attribute that is opposite to existence.
Correction: The author argues that even if necessity is privative, it is not opposite to existence; it is a mental concept, not a real attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the nature of necessity?
A) A real attribute distinct from existence.
B) A mental concept obtained from relating concepts to existence.
C) A privative attribute that negates existence.
D) An external existent that is an effect.

Key Takeaway
Necessity is a mental concept, not an external attribute; the privative objection fails because it relies on a false assumption of univocal existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author argues that necessity is a mental construct, not an external attribute. When you reflect on your own certainty about God's existence, do you base it on a mental category or on a direct existential relationship? What would change if you treated that certainty as a mere concept?
?
In your daily life, you often use the word 'necessary' for things like food, money, or relationships. Are these actually necessary in the absolute sense, or are you confusing mental concepts with true necessity? How does this affect your reliance on Allah?
?
The privative objection assumes that non-existence cannot necessitate existence. Look at your own heart: have you ever assumed that your lack (of knowledge, wealth, status) could never lead to something positive (like humility, need for Allah)? The author shows that privation can indeed necessitate something. How can you transform your perceived deficiencies into means of drawing closer to Allah?

Allah's Existence

The Impossibility of Sharing Necessity by Itself
Razi proves that necessity by itself cannot be shared using a reductio argument, and addresses objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessity by itself cannot be shared between two beings, and how Razi proves that shared necessity leads to composition and contingency.

Core Idea
Shared necessity makes a being composite, and every composite is contingent.

This lesson presents one of the central arguments in Razi's Muhassal: the proof that necessity by itself cannot be shared. Using a reductio ad absurdum, Razi shows that if necessity were shared, each necessary being would be composite—composed of a shared element and a distinguishing element—which would render it contingent, contradicting its necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the main argument
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the logical flow of the reductio.
The argument assumes saving necessity by itself cannot be shared.
2
Identify the reductio assumption
Razi begins by assuming the opposite: that necessity by itself is shared between two. What does this lead to?
3
Understand the composition argument
If shared, each being has a common part (the shared necessity) and a distinguishing part. This composition is the key.
Every composite is possible (contingent), which contradicts necessity.
4
Examine the two scenarios
Razi considers two possibilities: either the parts have no necessary connection, leading to an external cause, or they have a connection, leading to an infinite regress or circularity.
Both scenarios lead to absurdity.
5
Conclude the proof
The argument shows that sharing necessity is impossible. Razi also addresses objections and offers a solution via verbal homonymy.
This sets the stage for the marginal notes in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الوجوب بالذات لا يكون مشتركا بين الاثنين. وإلا لكان هو مغايرا لما به يمتاز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر فيكون كل واحد منهما مركبا عما به الاشتراك وما به الامتياز، فإن لم يكن بين الجزئية ملازمة كان اجتماعهما معلول علة منفصلة هذا خلف، وإن كان بينهما ملازمة فإن استلزمت الهوية للوجوب كان الوجوب معلول الغير هذا خلاف، وإن كان الوجوب مستلزما لتلك الهوية فكل واجب هو هو ما ليس هو لم يكن واجبا فقيل عليه بناء على كون الوجود وصفا ثبوتيا وهو باطل وإلا لكان داخلا في الماهية أو خارجا وكلاهما باطلان على ما تقدم، ولأنه لو كان ثبوتيا لكان مساويا في الثبوت كسائر الماهيات ومخالفا لها في خصوصيته فوجوده غير ماهيته فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إن كان واجبا كان الوجوب وجوب آخر إلى غير النهاية، وإن لم يكن واجبا كان ممكنا والواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا هذا خلف، وأيضا فهو مبني على كون التعين وصفا ثبوتيا زائدا وهو باطل على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى، وأيضا فهي معارضة بأن واجب الوجود مساو للممكن في الموجودية ومخالف له في الوجوب فوجوده ووجوبه متغايران ويعود التقسيم المذكور في أول الباب. وقد عرفت هناك أنه لا جواب إلا قولنا الموجود مقول على الواجب والممكن بالاشتراك اللفظي فقط وإذا كان كذلك فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الوجوب بالذات مقولا على الواجبين بالاشتراك اللفظي فقط. (1) أقول: جميع ما قاله في الاستدلال والمعارضة مبني على كون الوجوب أمرا موجودا عارضا للواجب، وقد مر بيان ما هو الحق فيه واعتبر ما أورده في المعارضة فإن وجوب القضايا لا يكون جزءاً من محمولاتها ولا من موضوعاتها بل يكون كيفية عقلية لانتساب محمولاتها إلى موضوعاتها، والكيفية العقلية لا تكون مستتبعة للأمور الخارجية بل تكون تابعا لها، ولا يلزم من كونها في ذاتها ممكنة كون ما يتعلق به من الأمور الخارجية ممكنة. وفي عبارة صاحب الكتاب هو فإن الواجب أن يقول: كيفيتان لانتساب المحمولات إلى الموضوعات. (2) أقول إن لزوم التركيب من تقدير كون الوجوب مشتركا بين اثنين كان الواجب أن يقتصر على ذلك لأنه قد تبين أن كل مركب ممكن. ثم قوله له بعد ذلك: فإن استلزمت الهوية الوجوب كان الوجوب معلول الغير هذا خلف فيه نظر، لأن الخلف لو كان الواجب معلول الغير لولا الوجوب أما إن كانت هويته مستلزمة لوجوبه وكان وجوبه محتاجا إلى هويته لم يلزم منه كون الهوية معلولا للغير، بل يلزم منه كون الهوية غير واجبة بانفرادها إنما تكون واجبة لصفة تقتضيها ذاتها، ولو قال في الأول الوجوب صفة فهي غير واجبة بدون الموصوف بها فيكون معلول الغير حصل مقصوده، والاعتراض عليه يكون الوجوب غير ثبوتي باطل على مذهبه، فإن نقيض اللاوجوب المحمول عليه العدم، فالوجوب يكون محمولا عليه. وقوله: وإن لم يكن الوجوب واجبا كان ممكنا فالواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا، إعادة المعنى وقد مر.
Issue: Necessity by itself cannot be shared between two. Otherwise it would be different from that by which each one is distinguished from the other, so each one would be composite of what is shared and what distinguishes. If there is no necessary connection between the parts, then their conjunction is an effect of a separate cause—this is a vicious circle. If there is a connection, then if the essence entails necessity, then necessity is an effect of another—this is contrary. If necessity entails that essence, then every necessary being that is itself what it is not would not be necessary. So it is said based on existence being a positive attribute, and that is false; otherwise it would be either inside the quiddity or outside, both false as previously. And because if it were positive, it would be equal in positivity to other quiddities but different in its specificity, so its existence is other than its quiddity. So the attribution of its quiddity by its existence: if it is necessary, then the necessity is another necessity ad infinitum; if it is not necessary, then it is possible, and the necessary by itself is more entitled to be possible—this is a vicious circle. Also, it is based on individuation being an additional positive attribute, which is false as will come. Also, it is opposed by the fact that the necessary of existence is equal to the possible in existence and different from it in necessity, so its existence and its necessity are different, and the division mentioned at the beginning of the chapter returns. And you have known there that there is no answer except our saying that 'existent' is predicated of the necessary and the possible only by verbal homonymy. If so, why is it not permissible for necessity by itself to be predicated of the two necessary beings only by verbal homonymy? (1) I say: All that he said in the proof and the objection is based on necessity being an existing attribute inhering in the necessary. The explanation of what is correct has passed. Consider what he presented in the objection: the necessity of propositions is not a part of their predicates nor of their subjects, but rather it is a mental quality of the attribution of their predicates to their subjects. The mental quality does not entail external matters but rather follows them. The fact that it is itself possible does not entail that what it pertains to from external matters is possible. In the wording of the author, he should say: two qualities for the attribution of predicates to subjects. (2) I say: The necessity of composition from supposing necessity is shared between two—he should have confined himself to that because it has been shown that every composite is possible. Then his statement after that: 'If the essence entails necessity, then necessity is an effect of another'—this is a vicious circle, but there is consideration. Because the vicious circle would be if the necessary were an effect of another without necessity. But if its essence entails its necessity and its necessity needs its essence, it does not necessitate that the essence is an effect of another, rather it necessitates that the essence is not necessary by itself, but becomes necessary due to an attribute required by its essence. If he had said in the first: 'Necessity is an attribute, so it is not necessary without the described, so it is an effect of another' he would have achieved his purpose. The objection against him that necessity is not positive is false according to his doctrine, because the opposite of non-necessity is non-existence predicated of it, so necessity is predicated of it. His statement: 'If necessity is not necessary, then it is possible, so the necessary by itself is more entitled to be possible'—this is a repetition of the meaning and has passed.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered argument on the impossibility of sharing necessity by itself between two beings. The main text begins with the thesis: necessity by itself cannot be shared. The proof proceeds by a reductio: if it were shared, each necessary being would be composite, having a common element (shared necessity) and a distinguishing element. This composition leads to contingency, because any composite is contingent. The author then examines two scenarios: either there is no necessary connection between the common and distinguishing parts, in which case their conjunction requires an external cause—a vicious circle; or there is a connection, leading to either necessity being an effect of the essence or the essence being entailed by necessity, both leading to absurdities. Additional arguments are given against the view that existence is a positive attribute, and an objection based on the equality of necessary and possible in existence is addressed. The author concludes that the only escape is to claim that 'existent' is predicated by homonymy, and similarly 'necessity by itself' can be predicated by homonymy. Then two marginal notes (marked with numbers) provide commentary. The first marginal note clarifies that the entire argument assumes necessity is an existing attribute inhering in the necessary, but actually necessity is a mental relation, not an extra-mental attribute, so the argument's premise is flawed. The second marginal note addresses a specific point about composition: if we suppose necessity is shared, composition follows, but the author could have stopped there; it also challenges the objection about essence entailing necessity, arguing that the essence might be necessary only through an attribute it requires, and that the claim that necessity is not positive is false because its opposite is non-existence.

Key Terms
الوجوب بالذات (wujūb bi-dhāt)
الاشتراك (ishtirāk)
التركيب (tarkīb)
الممكن (mumkin)
المعلول (ma‘lūl)
الخلف (khulf)
الوصف الثبوتي (waṣf thubūtī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that necessary beings share a common attribute of necessity.
Correction: The argument shows that shared necessity leads to composition and contingency, so necessity cannot be a common attribute.

Checkpoint
What is a consequence of necessity by itself being shared between two beings according to Razi's argument?
A) Both beings would be independent.
B) Each being would be composite and thus contingent.
C) The beings would be identical.
D) The necessity would be a mental quality.

Key Takeaway
Necessity by itself cannot be shared because it would make the necessary being composite, and every composite is contingent, contradicting necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If necessity by itself cannot be shared, then your entire existence depends on a Being whose necessity is absolutely unique. How does this fact reshape your understanding of your own dependence on Him? What practical difference does it make in your life today?
?
The argument shows that any shareable attribute would make the necessary being composite. In what ways do you still think of Allah as having parts or attributes that could be compared to others? How can you purify your tawhid starting today?
?
Razi concludes that 'existent' is predicated homonymously of the necessary and possible. Do you really believe that Allah's existence is absolutely different from your existence? If you did, how would it change your prayer, your trust, your fear?

Refutation of the Arguments: The Mental Nature of Necessity
Razi critiques the assumption that necessity is an existing attribute and clarifies its mental nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two critical marginal notes in which Razi clarifies that the previous arguments assume necessity is an existing attribute, whereas it is actually a mental quality, and he refines the composition argument.

Core Idea
Necessity is a mental relation, not an extra-mental attribute, so the earlier reductio's premise is flawed.

This lesson examines the two marginal notes appended to the main argument. In these notes, Razi critiques the assumption that necessity is an existing attribute inhering in the necessary being. He argues that necessity is a mental quality of propositions, not an extra-mental attribute. He also addresses a specific point about composition and the entailment between essence and necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the first marginal note
Focus on the claim that the entire argument is based on necessity being an existing attribute. Razi says the correct view is that necessity is a mental quality.
This shifts the ground of the argument.
2
Understand the mental quality
Necessity as a mental quality of attribution does not entail external matters. Its possibility does not imply the possibility of what it pertains to.
3
Read the second marginal note
Razi notes that the composition argument is sufficient; he then critiques the earlier objection about essence entailing necessity.
He shows that the essence might be necessary only through an attribute required by itself.
4
Grasp the refinement
If necessity is an attribute, it is not necessary without the described, so it is an effect of another. But the objection that necessity is not positive is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الوجوب بالذات لا يكون مشتركا بين الاثنين. وإلا لكان هو مغايرا لما به يمتاز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر فيكون كل واحد منهما مركبا عما به الاشتراك وما به الامتياز، فإن لم يكن بين الجزئية ملازمة كان اجتماعهما معلول علة منفصلة هذا خلف، وإن كان بينهما ملازمة فإن استلزمت الهوية للوجوب كان الوجوب معلول الغير هذا خلاف، وإن كان الوجوب مستلزما لتلك الهوية فكل واجب هو هو ما ليس هو لم يكن واجبا فقيل عليه بناء على كون الوجود وصفا ثبوتيا وهو باطل وإلا لكان داخلا في الماهية أو خارجا وكلاهما باطلان على ما تقدم، ولأنه لو كان ثبوتيا لكان مساويا في الثبوت كسائر الماهيات ومخالفا لها في خصوصيته فوجوده غير ماهيته فاتصاف ماهيته بوجوده إن كان واجبا كان الوجوب وجوب آخر إلى غير النهاية، وإن لم يكن واجبا كان ممكنا والواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا هذا خلف، وأيضا فهو مبني على كون التعين وصفا ثبوتيا زائدا وهو باطل على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى، وأيضا فهي معارضة بأن واجب الوجود مساو للممكن في الموجودية ومخالف له في الوجوب فوجوده ووجوبه متغايران ويعود التقسيم المذكور في أول الباب. وقد عرفت هناك أنه لا جواب إلا قولنا الموجود مقول على الواجب والممكن بالاشتراك اللفظي فقط وإذا كان كذلك فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الوجوب بالذات مقولا على الواجبين بالاشتراك اللفظي فقط. (1) أقول: جميع ما قاله في الاستدلال والمعارضة مبني على كون الوجوب أمرا موجودا عارضا للواجب، وقد مر بيان ما هو الحق فيه واعتبر ما أورده في المعارضة فإن وجوب القضايا لا يكون جزءاً من محمولاتها ولا من موضوعاتها بل يكون كيفية عقلية لانتساب محمولاتها إلى موضوعاتها، والكيفية العقلية لا تكون مستتبعة للأمور الخارجية بل تكون تابعا لها، ولا يلزم من كونها في ذاتها ممكنة كون ما يتعلق به من الأمور الخارجية ممكنة. وفي عبارة صاحب الكتاب هو فإن الواجب أن يقول: كيفيتان لانتساب المحمولات إلى الموضوعات. (2) أقول إن لزوم التركيب من تقدير كون الوجوب مشتركا بين اثنين كان الواجب أن يقتصر على ذلك لأنه قد تبين أن كل مركب ممكن. ثم قوله له بعد ذلك: فإن استلزمت الهوية الوجوب كان الوجوب معلول الغير هذا خلف فيه نظر، لأن الخلف لو كان الواجب معلول الغير لولا الوجوب أما إن كانت هويته مستلزمة لوجوبه وكان وجوبه محتاجا إلى هويته لم يلزم منه كون الهوية معلولا للغير، بل يلزم منه كون الهوية غير واجبة بانفرادها إنما تكون واجبة لصفة تقتضيها ذاتها، ولو قال في الأول الوجوب صفة فهي غير واجبة بدون الموصوف بها فيكون معلول الغير حصل مقصوده، والاعتراض عليه يكون الوجوب غير ثبوتي باطل على مذهبه، فإن نقيض اللاوجوب المحمول عليه العدم، فالوجوب يكون محمولا عليه. وقوله: وإن لم يكن الوجوب واجبا كان ممكنا فالواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون ممكنا، إعادة المعنى وقد مر.
Issue: Necessity by itself cannot be shared between two. Otherwise it would be different from that by which each one is distinguished from the other, so each one would be composite of what is shared and what distinguishes. If there is no necessary connection between the parts, then their conjunction is an effect of a separate cause—this is a vicious circle. If there is a connection, then if the essence entails necessity, then necessity is an effect of another—this is contrary. If necessity entails that essence, then every necessary being that is itself what it is not would not be necessary. So it is said based on existence being a positive attribute, and that is false; otherwise it would be either inside the quiddity or outside, both false as previously. And because if it were positive, it would be equal in positivity to other quiddities but different in its specificity, so its existence is other than its quiddity. So the attribution of its quiddity by its existence: if it is necessary, then the necessity is another necessity ad infinitum; if it is not necessary, then it is possible, and the necessary by itself is more entitled to be possible—this is a vicious circle. Also, it is based on individuation being an additional positive attribute, which is false as will come. Also, it is opposed by the fact that the necessary of existence is equal to the possible in existence and different from it in necessity, so its existence and its necessity are different, and the division mentioned at the beginning of the chapter returns. And you have known there that there is no answer except our saying that 'existent' is predicated of the necessary and the possible only by verbal homonymy. If so, why is it not permissible for necessity by itself to be predicated of the two necessary beings only by verbal homonymy? (1) I say: All that he said in the proof and the objection is based on necessity being an existing attribute inhering in the necessary. The explanation of what is correct has passed. Consider what he presented in the objection: the necessity of propositions is not a part of their predicates nor of their subjects, but rather it is a mental quality of the attribution of their predicates to their subjects. The mental quality does not entail external matters but rather follows them. The fact that it is itself possible does not entail that what it pertains to from external matters is possible. In the wording of the author, he should say: two qualities for the attribution of predicates to subjects. (2) I say: The necessity of composition from supposing necessity is shared between two—he should have confined himself to that because it has been shown that every composite is possible. Then his statement after that: 'If the essence entails necessity, then necessity is an effect of another'—this is a vicious circle, but there is consideration. Because the vicious circle would be if the necessary were an effect of another without necessity. But if its essence entails its necessity and its necessity needs its essence, it does not necessitate that the essence is an effect of another, rather it necessitates that the essence is not necessary by itself, but becomes necessary due to an attribute required by its essence. If he had said in the first: 'Necessity is an attribute, so it is not necessary without the described, so it is an effect of another' he would have achieved his purpose. The objection against him that necessity is not positive is false according to his doctrine, because the opposite of non-necessity is non-existence predicated of it, so necessity is predicated of it. His statement: 'If necessity is not necessary, then it is possible, so the necessary by itself is more entitled to be possible'—this is a repetition of the meaning and has passed.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered argument on the impossibility of sharing necessity by itself between two beings. The main text begins with the thesis: necessity by itself cannot be shared. The proof proceeds by a reductio: if it were shared, each necessary being would be composite, having a common element (shared necessity) and a distinguishing element. This composition leads to contingency, because any composite is contingent. The author then examines two scenarios: either there is no necessary connection between the common and distinguishing parts, in which case their conjunction requires an external cause—a vicious circle; or there is a connection, leading to either necessity being an effect of the essence or the essence being entailed by necessity, both leading to absurdities. Additional arguments are given against the view that existence is a positive attribute, and an objection based on the equality of necessary and possible in existence is addressed. The author concludes that the only escape is to claim that 'existent' is predicated by homonymy, and similarly 'necessity by itself' can be predicated by homonymy. Then two marginal notes (marked with numbers) provide commentary. The first marginal note clarifies that the entire argument assumes necessity is an existing attribute inhering in the necessary, but actually necessity is a mental relation, not an extra-mental attribute, so the argument's premise is flawed. The second marginal note addresses a specific point about composition: if we suppose necessity is shared, composition follows, but the author could have stopped there; it also challenges the objection about essence entailing necessity, arguing that the essence might be necessary only through an attribute it requires, and that the claim that necessity is not positive is false because its opposite is non-existence.

Key Terms
الكيفية العقلية (kayfiyya ‘aqliyya)
الاشتراك (ishtirāk)
الوجوب (wujūb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think necessity is an existing attribute inherent in the necessary being.
Correction: Razi clarifies necessity is a mental quality of propositions, not an extra-mental attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the first marginal note, what is the nature of the necessity of propositions?
A) An existing attribute inhering in the subject.
B) A mental quality of the attribution of predicates to subjects.
C) A part of the predicate.
D) An extra-mental relation.

Key Takeaway
Razi critiques the assumption that necessity is an existing attribute, clarifying it is a mental quality, and refines the composition argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You likely hold many assumptions about God's existence without examining their logical basis. This passage shows that even scholars like Razi scrutinize every premise. Where in your own belief system have you avoided such scrutiny? Will you now revisit one assumption you had never questioned?
?
The passage distinguishes between mental qualities and external reality. Are you ever guilty of treating your own mental constructs (like necessity or causality) as if they were absolute external truths? How might this affect your understanding of God's oneness?
?
Razi's argument hinges on the idea that necessity is a mental attribution, not an existing attribute. If God's necessity is merely a mental relation, does that shake your confidence in rational proofs for God? How will you respond to that discomfort? Will you seek deeper understanding or retreat into comfort?

Allah's Existence
advanced
10 min
The word 'wajib' is applied by homonymy
Razi argues that 'wajib' is used homonymously for necessary-by-itself and necessary-by-another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'wajib' must be used homonymously for the Necessary-by-itself and the Necessary-by-another, and why univocal predication would compromise God's absolute simplicity.

Core Idea
The term 'wajib' is used homonymously to avoid making the Necessary-by-itself composite and thus contingent.

In this dense passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi tackles a subtle logical issue: can the same word 'wajib' mean the same thing when applied to the Necessary-by-itself (God) and to something that is necessary due to another? The mainstream view he defends is that it is used by verbal homonymy (اشتراك لفظي), not by univocality (اشتراك معنوي). This is not a mere terminological quibble; it safeguards God's absolute simplicity and necessity. The passage presents multiple arguments and responses, including a critique of those who deny that necessity is a positive attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement and dilemma
Start by reading the initial claim that 'wajib' is used homonymously, followed by the first argument: if it were univocal, the Necessary-by-itself would be composite and thus contingent. Notice the dilemma about the common concept being independent or dependent.
This is the core logical move.
2
Examine the objection from division
Consider the objection that one can divide 'wajib' into two types, so the term must be common. Then see how Razi deals with this objection.
The objector uses the principle that the subject of division is univocal.
3
Understand the argument against positive attribute
Follow the argument that if 'wajib' were a positive attribute, it would have to be univocal or homonymous, both of which are claimed false, so existence is not a positive attribute. Note Razi's critique.
4
Follow the philosopher's argument about predication
Read the alternative argument: the Necessary-by-itself cannot be predicated of two beings because it leads to composition and contingency. Understand the classification into essential vs. accidental.
This is a more rigorous argument from the philosophers.
5
Study the marginal note's clarification
Finally, read the marginal note which responds to potential misunderstandings, clarifying that composition in the concept does not mean composition in the subject, and that the dilemma's second part does not necessarily lead to a vicious circle.
The note also draws an analogy with impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: وقوع لفظ الواجب على الواجب بالذات والواجب بالغير بالاشتراك اللفظي. وإلا فالوجوب بالذات مركب فيكون ممكنا ولأن القدر المشترك إن كان غنيا عن الغير لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالغير عارضا للغير هذا خلف، وإن كان مفتقرا لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالذات غنيا عن الغير فمعارض بأن مسمى الوجوب يمكن تقسيمه إلى الواجب بالذات وإلى الواجب بالغير ومورد التقسيم مشترك بين القسمين لا محالة، والقائل أن يستدل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفا ثبوتيا بأنه لو كان وصفا ثبوتيا لكان إما أن يكون مقولا على الواجب بالذات والواجب بالغير بالاشتراك المعنوي أو بالاشتراك اللفظي وهما باطلان على ما تقدم فالوجود ليس وصفا ثبوتيا (1). من الكلام عليه، والمعارضة بكون الواجب مساويا للممكن في الوجود فقد بينا أن اشتراكهما في الوجود ليس بالتواطؤ، والمهرب الذي هرب إليه أخيرا إن الوجوب بالذات مقول على الواجبين بالاشتراك اللفظي لا ينجيه هذه الحيرة، وإنه من غاية التحير لا يدري إلى أي شيء يتأدى كلامه ولا يبالي بالتناقض ولا الإلزام ما لا يخلصه من حيرته، وكان من الواجب أن يقول كما قال غيره من الحكماء: الواجب لذاته يستحيل أن يكون محمولا على اثنين لأنه إما أن يكون ذاتيا لهما أو عرضيا لهما أو ذاتيا لأحدهما عرضيا للآخر فإن كان ذاتيا لهما فالخصوصية التي بها يمتاز كل واحد من الآخر لا يمكن أن يكون داخلا في المعنى المشترك، وإلا فلا امتياز فهو خارج فينضاف إلى المعنى المشترك، فإن كان في كل واحدة منهما كان كل واحدة منهما ممكنة من حيث هو موجود وممتاز من الآخر، وإن كان في أحدهما فهو ممكن وإن كان عرضا لهما أو لأحدهما فمعروضه لا يكون واجبا لا يقال الواجب المعنى المشترك فقط لأنا بينا أن المعنى المشترك لا يوجد في الخارج من حيث هو مشترك من غير تخصيص يزيل اشتراكه، فإن قيل المخصص سلي وكل واحد منهما مختص بأنه ليس الآخر قلنا سلب الغير لا يتحصل إلا بعد حصول الغير وحينئذ يكون كل واحد هو هو بعد حصول الغير فيكون ممكنا وفيه كفاية في هذا المطلوب. (1) أقول: لا يلزم من كون الوجوب مشتركا بين الوجوب بالذات والوجوب بالغير كون الوجوب بالذات لا يفتقر إلى تعقل غير الذات، أما الوجوب بالغير فيفتقر تعقله إلى انضمام تعقل الغير وإلى تعقل الوجوب، ثم لو كان الوجوب الذي هو أمر يحصل في العقل عند إسناد متصور إلى الوجود الخارجي مركبا لم يلزم منه تركيب المسند إليه، كما لا يلزم من كونه محتاجا إلى موصوف به كون الموصوف به محتاجا إلى غيره، وأيضاً الامتناع أيضاً مشترك بين الامتناع بالذات والامتناع بالغير، ولا يجب من تركيبه تركب في الممتنع لذاته الذي يكون منفيا محضا. وقوله في الوجه الثاني: القدر المشترك إن كان غنيا من الغير لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالغير عارضا للغير هذا خلف فيه نظر، لأنه لا يلزم منه الخلف، فإن من استغناء الجزء لا يلزم استغناء المركب، بل إنما يلزم من افتقار الجزء افتقار المركب، والمعارضة التي أوردها حجة على الاشتراك المعنوي في الوجوب واستدلاله على كون الوجوب غير ثبوتي باطل ما مر.
Issue: The word 'wajib' applies to the necessary by itself and the necessary by another by verbal homonymy. Otherwise, the necessity by itself would be composite and thus possible. And because the common concept, if it were independent of another, would not be the entire quiddity of the necessary by another as inhering in another—this is a vicious circle; and if it were dependent, it would not be the entire quiddity of the necessary by itself as independent of another. So it is objected that the meaning of 'wajib' can be divided into necessary by itself and necessary by another, and the subject of division is necessarily common between the two divisions. The one who argues that necessity is not a positive attribute says: if it were a positive attribute, it would be predicated of the necessary by itself and the necessary by another either by univocality or by homonymy, and both are false as previously, so existence is not a positive attribute (1). From the discourse on it, the objection is that the necessary is equal to the possible in existence, and we have shown that their sharing in existence is not by univocality. The escape he finally escaped to—that necessity by itself is predicated of the two necessary beings by verbal homonymy—does not save him from this perplexity. He, from the utmost bewilderment, does not know to what his speech leads, and he does not care about contradiction or entailment that would not save him from his perplexity. It was incumbent upon him to say, as other philosophers said: The necessary by itself cannot be predicated of two, because either it is essential to both, or accidental to both, or essential to one and accidental to the other. If it is essential to both, then the specificity by which each is distinguished from the other cannot be included in the common meaning; otherwise there is no distinction, so it is external and is added to the common meaning. If it is in each of them, then each of them is possible insofar as it is existent and distinct from the other. If it is in one of them, then it is possible. If it is accidental to both or to one, then its subject is not necessary. It cannot be said that the necessary is only the common meaning, because we have shown that the common meaning does not exist in the exterior insofar as it is common without specification that removes its commonness. If it is said: the specification is negative, and each one is specified by being not the other, we say: the negation of the other is only realized after the existence of the other, and then each one is itself after the existence of the other, so it is possible. In this is sufficiency for this objective. (1) I say: The fact that 'wajib' is shared between the necessary by itself and the necessary by another does not necessitate that the necessary by itself does not need the conception of another. The necessary by another, its conception needs the addition of the conception of another and the conception of necessity. Then if the necessity which is something obtained in the mind when a conceived thing is attributed to external existence were composite, it would not necessitate composition of the subject of attribution, just as the fact that it needs a described does not necessitate that the described needs another. Also, impossibility is also shared between impossibility by itself and impossibility by another, and its composition does not necessitate composition in the impossible by itself which is pure negation. His statement in the second aspect: 'The common concept, if it were independent of another, would not be the entire quiddity of the necessary by another as inhering in another—this is a vicious circle'—there is consideration in this, because the vicious circle does not follow from it. The independence of a part does not necessitate the independence of the whole, rather only dependence of a part necessitates dependence of the whole. The objection he presented is an argument for univocality in necessity, and his proof that necessity is not positive is false as passed.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses whether the word 'wajib' (necessary) is used univocally or homonymously for the necessary-by-itself and the necessary-by-another. The main text argues that it must be by verbal homonymy, because if it were univocal, the necessary-by-itself would be composite (having a common concept and a distinguishing feature) and thus contingent. It presents a dilemma: if the common concept is independent of another, it cannot be the full quiddity of the necessary-by-another which inheres in another; if it is dependent, it cannot be the full quiddity of the necessary-by-itself which is independent. An objection is raised that the term 'wajib' can be divided into the two types, so the subject of division must be common—this supports univocality. The author then discusses someone who argues that necessity is not a positive attribute, and shows the inadequacy of the escape that it is merely homonymous. He goes on to present a more rigorous argument from the philosophers: the necessary-by-itself cannot be predicated of two because it would have to be either essential or accidental to both or one, leading to composition and contingency. It cannot even be said that the necessary is just the common meaning, because the common meaning does not exist without specification. The marginal note responds that sharing necessity does not make the necessary-by-itself dependent on conceiving another; it only makes the necessary-by-another dependent. Also, composition in the mental concept of necessity does not entail composition in the subject. The marginal note also addresses the second aspect of the dilemma, arguing that the independence of a part does not imply independence of the whole, so the vicious circle does not hold.

Key Terms
الاشتراك اللفظي (ishtirāk lafẓī)
الاشتراك المعنوي (ishtirāk ma‘nawī)
الواجب بالذات (wājib bi-dhāt)
الواجب بالغير (wājib bi-ghayr)
القدر المشترك (qadr mushtarak)
العرض (‘araḍ)
الذاتي (dhātī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'necessary' has the same meaning for both the Necessary-by-itself and the Necessary-by-another, i.e., univocal use.
Correction: The passage argues that univocal use would make the Necessary-by-itself composite and thus contingent, which is impossible. Therefore, the term must be used homonymously.

Checkpoint
According to the main argument in this passage, why must the term 'wajib' be used by homonymy?
A) Because necessary-by-itself and necessary-by-another share the same meaning.
B) Because if it were univocal, the necessary-by-itself would be composite and thus contingent.
C) Because the necessary-by-itself does not need another.
D) Because the common concept is independent.

Key Takeaway
The term 'wajib' is used homonymously to avoid attributing composition to the Necessary-by-itself, thereby preserving its absolute necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you think of Allah as 'Necessary', do you unconsciously compare His necessity to the necessity of other things you depend on (like food or water)? What would change in your reliance on Him if you truly believed His necessity is absolutely unique?

This lesson warns that making the concept of wajib composite would make God possible. Do you ever, even unintentionally, imagine God as having 'parts'—for example, a separate essence and attributes? How can you purify your understanding of Tawḥīd starting today?

The Homonymous Use of 'Wajib' and the Dilemma of the Common Factor
Razi asserts homonymy and presents a dilemma against univocality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'wajib' is used homonymously for necessary by essence and necessary by other, and how an argument about a common factor leads to a contradiction if it were univocal.

Core Idea
The word 'wajib' does not mean the same for necessary by essence and necessary by other.

Imam Razi begins by asserting that the term 'wajib' is used homonymously (ishtirak lafzi) for necessary by essence and necessary by other. He then provides a concise argument: if it were univocal, necessity by essence would become composite, leading to impossibility. This passage lays the foundation for a deeper debate about the nature of necessity and its application to different entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim and its conditional
Start by reading the first sentence where Razi states the homonymous use. Then notice the conditional 'otherwise' (wa illa) and the immediate consequence that necessity by essence would be composite and possible.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum structure.
2
Analyze the dilemma of the common factor
Razi presents a dilemma: if the common factor (al-qadr al-mushtarak) is independent of the other, then it cannot be the entire quiddity of necessity by other; if dependent, it cannot be the entire quiddity of necessity by essence. Both lead to contradiction.
The word 'ghani' (independent) is key here.
3
Connect to the overall issue
Reflect that this argument shows that univocal predication of 'wajib' yields logical contradictions, supporting the homonymous interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : وقوع لفظ الواجب على الواجب بالذات والواجب بالغير بالاشتراك اللفظى . وإلا فالوجوب بالذات مركب فيكون ممكنا ولأن القدر المشترك إن كان غنيا عن الغير لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالغير عارضا للغير هذا خلف، وإن كان مفتقرا لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالذات غنيا عن الغير. فمورض بأن مسمى الوجوب يمكن تقسيمه إلى الواجب بالذات وإلى الواجب بالغير ومورد التقسيم مشترك بين القسمين لا محالة. والقائل أن يستدل على أن الوجوب ليس وصفا ثبوتيا بأنه لو كان وصفا ثبوتيا لمكان إما أن يكون مقولا على الواجب بالذات والواجب بالغير بالاشتراك المعنوى أو بالاشتراك اللفظ وهما باطلان على ما تقدم فالوجود ليس وصفا ثبوتيا. والمعارضة بكون الواجب مساويا للممكن فى الوجود فقد بينا أن اشتراكهما في الوجود ليس بالتواطؤ. والمهرب الذى هرب إليه أخيرا إن الوجوب بالذات مقول على الواجبين بالاشتراك اللفظى لا ينجيه هذه الحيرة، وإنه من غاية التحير لا يدرى إلى أى شىء يتأدى كلامه ولا يبالى بالتناقض ولا الإلزام مالا يخلصه من حيرته. وكان من الواجب أن يقول كما قال غيره من الحكماء : الواجب لذاته يستحيل أن يكون محمولا على اثنين لأنه إما أن يكون ذاتيا لهما أو عرضيا لهما أو ذاتيا لأحدهما عرضيا للآخر. فإن كان ذاتيا لهما فالخصوصية التي بها يمتاز كل واحد من الآخر لا يمكن أن يكون داخلا في المعنى المشترك. وإلا فلا امتياز فهو خارج فينضاف إلى المعنى المشترك. فإن كان فى كل واحدة منهما كان كل واحدة منهما ممكنة من حيث هو موجود وممتاز من الآخر. وإن كان فى أحدهما فهو ممكن. وإن كان عرضا لهما أو لأحدهما فمعروضه لا يكون واجبا. لا يقال الواجب المعنى المشترك فقط لأنا بينا أن المعنى المشترك لا يوجد في الخارج من حيث هو مشترك من غير تخصيص يزيل اشتراكه. فإن قيل المخصص سلب وكل واحد منهما مختص بأنه ليس الآخر. قلنا سلب الغير لا يتحصل إلا بعد حصول الغير وحينئذ يكون كل واحد هو هو بعد حصول الغير فيكون ممكنا. وفيه كفاية في هذا المطلوب . أقول : لا يلزم من كون الوجوب مشتركا بين الوجوب بالذات والوجوب بالغير كون الوجوب بالذات لا يفتقر إلى تعقل غير الذات، أما الوجوب بالغير فيفتقر تعقله إلى انضياف تعقل الغير وإلى تعقل الوجوب. ثم لو كان الوجوب الذى هو أمر يحصل في العقل عند إسناد متصور إلى الوجود الخارجى مركبا لم يلزم منه تركيب المسند إليه. كما لا يلزم من كونه محتاجا إلى موصوف به كون الموصوف به محتاجا إلى غيره. وأيضاً الامتناع أيضاً مشترك بين الامتناع بالذات والامتناع بالغير، ولا يجب من تركيبه تركب في الممتنع لذاته الذى يكون منعا محضا. وقوله في الوجه الثانى : القدر المشترك إن كان غنيا من الغير لم يكن تمام ماهية الوجوب بالغير عارضا للغير هذا خلف. فيه نظر، لأنه لا يلزم منه الخلف، فإن من استغناء الجزء لا يلزم استغناء المركب، بل إنما يلزم من افتقار الجزء افتقار المركب. والمعارضة التي أوردها حجة على الاشتراك المعنوى في الوجوب. واستدلاله على كون الوجوب غير ثبوتى باطل كما مر.
Issue: The occurrence of the word 'wajib' upon the necessary by essence and the necessary by other is by homonymy. Otherwise, the necessity by essence would be composite and thus possible. And because the common factor, if it were independent of the other, would not be the entire quiddity of the necessity by other being an accident of the other—this is a contradiction. And if it were dependent, it would not be the entire quiddity of the necessity by essence independent of the other. So it is objected that the named 'necessity' can be divided into the necessary by essence and the necessary by other, and the subject of division is shared between the two divisions necessarily. And the objector argues that necessity is not a positive attribute because if it were a positive attribute, then it would be predicated of the necessary by essence and the necessary by other either by univocal homonymy or by equivocal homonymy, and both are invalid as previously mentioned. So existence is not a positive attribute. And the objection that the necessary is equal to the possible in existence—we have shown that their sharing in existence is not by univocality. The escape which he finally escapes to, that necessity by essence is predicated of the two necessaries by equivocal homonymy, does not save him from this perplexity. He is in extreme confusion: he does not know to what his speech leads, nor does he care about contradiction or implication that does not release him from his confusion. He ought to have said, as other philosophers said: The necessary by essence cannot be predicated of two, because it is either essential for both, accidental for both, or essential for one and accidental for the other. If it is essential for both, then the particularity by which each is distinguished from the other cannot be included in the common meaning; otherwise there would be no distinction. So it is outside and is added to the common meaning. If it is in each of them, then each of them is possible insofar as it exists and is distinguished from the other. If it is in one of them, then it is possible. If it is accidental for both or for one, then its subject cannot be necessary. It cannot be said that the necessary is only the common meaning, because we have shown that the common meaning does not exist externally insofar as it is common without a specification removing its commonality. If it is said: The specification is negation, and each one is specified by not being the other. We say: The negation of the other is only obtained after the obtaining of the other. Then each one is itself after the obtaining of the other, and thus it is possible. And in this is sufficiency for this purpose. I say: From the fact that necessity is shared between necessity by essence and necessity by other, it does not follow that necessity by essence does not require conceptualization of something other than the essence. As for necessity by other, its conceptualization requires adding conceptualization of the other and conceptualization of necessity. Furthermore, if necessity, which is something that occurs in the mind when a conceived thing is attributed to external existence, were composite, it would not follow from that composition in the subject of attribution. Just as, from its being needful of something described by it, it does not follow that the described thing is needful of something else. Also, impossibility is also shared between impossibility by essence and impossibility by other, and its composition does not necessitate composition in the impossible by essence, which is pure negation. And his statement in the second aspect: 'The common factor, if it were independent of the other, would not be the entire quiddity of the necessity by other being an accident of the other—this is a contradiction.' There is consideration in it, because the contradiction does not follow from it. For from the independence of the part, the independence of the composite does not follow; rather, from the dependence of the part, the dependence of the composite follows. And the objection he raised is an argument for univocal homonymy in necessity. And his inference that necessity is not positive is invalid as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a complex issue about the term 'wajib' (necessary) and whether it applies univocally or equivocally to necessary by essence (wājib bi al-dhāt) and necessary by other (wājib bi al-ghayr). The author begins by stating that the word is used by homonymy (al-ishtirāk al-lafẓī). He then argues that if it were univocal, necessity by essence would be composite, leading to impossibility. The argument proceeds through a dialectic: a common factor (al-qadr al-mushtarak) is considered; if independent, it cannot be the entire quiddity of necessity by other; if dependent, it cannot be the entire quiddity of necessity by essence. An objector (al-qā'il) argues that necessity is not a positive attribute (waṣf thubūtī) because if it were, it would be predicated of both either univocally or equivocally, both invalid. The author then criticizes this objector's escape to equivocal homonymy as insufficient, and presents the correct view of the philosophers: the necessary by essence cannot be predicated of two, and he provides a logical analysis based on essential and accidental predication. The passage concludes with the author's own commentary ('aqūl) clarifying that the shared nature of necessity does not entail composition in the necessary by essence, and that the objector's inference that necessity is not positive is invalid.

Key Terms
واجب بالذات
واجب بالغير
اشتراك لفظي
قدر مشترك
وجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'wajib' is used in the same sense for necessary by essence and necessary by other.
Correction: This passage shows that univocal use leads to logical contradictions, so the correct position is homonymous use.

Checkpoint
What is the main claim at the beginning of this passage regarding the word 'wajib'?
A) It is used univocally for necessary by essence and necessary by other.
B) It is used homonymously for necessary by essence and necessary by other.
C) It is used metaphorically.
D) It is used only for necessary by essence.

Key Takeaway
The term 'wajib' is used homonymously, and any attempt to treat it univocally leads to logical contradictions.
